</div>
</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reign">Reign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Reign">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Burgundy_and_the_Low_Countries">Burgundy and the Low Countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Burgundy and the Low Countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Empire-Roman-Emperor-Charles-V.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Empire-Roman-Emperor-Charles-V.jpg/220px-Empire-Roman-Emperor-Charles-V.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Empire-Roman-Emperor-Charles-V.jpg/330px-Empire-Roman-Emperor-Charles-V.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Empire-Roman-Emperor-Charles-V.jpg/440px-Empire-Roman-Emperor-Charles-V.jpg 2x" data-file-width="665" data-file-height="458" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Empire-Roman-Emperor-Charles-V.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Charles V's European territories. Red represents the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Crown of Aragon</a>, magenta the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a>, orange his <a href="/wiki/House_of_Valois-Burgundy" title="House of Valois-Burgundy">Burgundian inheritances</a>, mustard yellow his <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Austrian inheritances</a>, and pale yellow the balance of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1506, Charles inherited his father's Burgundian territories, most notably the Low Countries and <a href="/wiki/Franche-Comt%C3%A9" title="Franche-Comté">Franche-Comté</a>. Most of the holdings were fiefs of the German Kingdom (part of the Holy Roman Empire), except his birthplace of Flanders, which was still a French fief, a last remnant of what had been a powerful player in the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Hundred Years' War">Hundred Years' War</a>. As he was a minor, his aunt <a href="/wiki/Margaret_of_Austria_(1480-1530)" class="mw-redirect" title="Margaret of Austria (1480-1530)">Margaret of Austria</a> (born as Archduchess of Austria and in both her marriages as the Dowager Princess of Asturias and Dowager Duchess of Savoy) acted as regent, as appointed by Emperor Maximilian until 1515. She soon found herself at war with France over the question of Charles' requirement to pay homage to the French king for Flanders, as his father had done. The outcome was that France relinquished its ancient claim on Flanders in 1528.</p>
<p>From 1515 to 1523, Charles's government in the Netherlands also had to contend with the rebellion of <a href="/wiki/Arumer_Zwarte_Hoop" title="Arumer Zwarte Hoop">Frisian peasants</a> (led by <a href="/wiki/Pier_Gerlofs_Donia" title="Pier Gerlofs Donia">Pier Gerlofs Donia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wijard_Jelckama" class="mw-redirect" title="Wijard Jelckama">Wijard Jelckama</a>). The rebels were initially successful but after a series of defeats, the remaining leaders were captured and decapitated in 1523.</p>
<p>Charles extended the Burgundian territory with the annexation of <a href="/wiki/Tournaisis" title="Tournaisis">Tournai</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_of_Artois" title="County of Artois">Artois</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Utrecht" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishopric of Utrecht">Utrecht</a>, <a href="/wiki/Groningen_(province)" title="Groningen (province)">Groningen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guelders" title="Guelders">Guelders</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Seventeen_Provinces" title="Seventeen Provinces">Seventeen Provinces</a> had been unified by Charles's Burgundian ancestors, but nominally were <a href="/wiki/Fief" title="Fief">fiefs</a> of either France or the Holy Roman Empire. In 1549, Charles issued a <a href="/wiki/Pragmatic_Sanction_of_1549" title="Pragmatic Sanction of 1549">Pragmatic Sanction</a>, declaring the Low Countries to be a unified entity of which his family would be the heirs.<sup id="cite_ref-Kamen_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kamen-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Low Countries held an important place in the Empire. For Charles V personally they were his home, the region where he was born and spent his childhood. Because of trade and industry and the wealth of the region's cities, the Low Countries also represented an important income for the Imperial treasury.</p>
<p>The Burgundian territories were generally loyal to Charles throughout his reign. The important city of Ghent <a href="/wiki/Revolt_of_Ghent_(1539)" title="Revolt of Ghent (1539)">rebelled</a> in 1539 due to heavy tax payments demanded by Charles. The rebellion did not last long, however, as Charles's military response, with reinforcement from the <a href="/wiki/Fernando_%C3%81lvarez_de_Toledo,_3rd_Duke_of_Alba" title="Fernando Álvarez de Toledo, 3rd Duke of Alba">Duke of Alba</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Kamen_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kamen-15">[15]</a></sup> was swift and humiliating to the rebels of Ghent.<sup id="cite_ref-Gentenaars_Stropdragers_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gentenaars_Stropdragers-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Toledo_Skyline_Panorama,_Spain_-_Dec_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Toledo_Skyline_Panorama%2C_Spain_-_Dec_2006.jpg/220px-Toledo_Skyline_Panorama%2C_Spain_-_Dec_2006.jpg" width="220" height="104" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Toledo_Skyline_Panorama%2C_Spain_-_Dec_2006.jpg/330px-Toledo_Skyline_Panorama%2C_Spain_-_Dec_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Toledo_Skyline_Panorama%2C_Spain_-_Dec_2006.jpg/440px-Toledo_Skyline_Panorama%2C_Spain_-_Dec_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4215" data-file-height="2002" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Toledo_Skyline_Panorama,_Spain_-_Dec_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The city of <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Spain" title="Toledo, Spain">Toledo</a> was the imperial capital and main seat of Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor, and his court.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-toledoescorte_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-toledoescorte-19">[19]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_Carlos_V_west.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Palacio_Carlos_V_west.jpg/220px-Palacio_Carlos_V_west.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Palacio_Carlos_V_west.jpg/330px-Palacio_Carlos_V_west.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Palacio_Carlos_V_west.jpg/440px-Palacio_Carlos_V_west.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_Carlos_V_west.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Exterior of The <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Charles_V" title="Palace of Charles V">Palace of Charles V</a> in Granada, built by Emperor Charles V upon his wedding to <a href="/wiki/Isabel_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Isabel of Portugal">Isabel of Portugal</a> in 1526.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the Castilian <i>Cortes</i> of Valladolid in 1506 and of Madrid in 1510, Charles was sworn as the <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Asturias" title="Prince of Asturias">Prince of Asturias</a>, heir-apparent to his mother the Queen <a href="/wiki/Joanna_of_Castile" title="Joanna of Castile">Joanna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> On the other hand, in 1502, the Aragonese <i>Corts</i> gathered in Saragossa and pledged an oath to Joanna as heiress-presumptive, but the Archbishop of Saragossa expressed firmly that this oath could not establish jurisprudence, that is to say, modify the right of the succession, except by virtue of a formal agreement between the <i>Cortes</i> and the King.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> So, upon the death of King Ferdinand II of Aragon, on 23 January 1516, Joanna inherited the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Crown of Aragon</a>, which consisted of <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Catalonia" title="Principality of Catalonia">Catalonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Valencia" title="Kingdom of Valencia">Valencia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Naples" title="Kingdom of Naples">Naples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sicily" title="Kingdom of Sicily">Sicily</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a>, while Charles became Governor General.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Nevertheless, the Flemings wished Charles to assume the royal title,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and this was supported by his grandfather the emperor <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Maximilian I, Holy Roman Emperor">Maximilian I</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_X" title="Pope Leo X">Pope Leo X</a>.</p>
<p>Thus, after the celebration of Ferdinand II's obsequies on 14 March 1516, Charles was proclaimed king of the crowns of Castile and Aragon jointly with his mother. Finally, when the Castilian <a href="/wiki/Regent" title="Regent">regent</a> Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Cisneros" class="mw-redirect" title="Jiménez de Cisneros">Jiménez de Cisneros</a> accepted the <i>fait accompli</i>, he acceded to Charles's desire to be proclaimed king and imposed his enstatement throughout the kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Charles arrived in his new kingdoms in autumn of 1517. Jiménez de Cisneros came to meet him but fell ill along the way, not without a suspicion of poison, and he died before meeting the King.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pantoja_de_la_Cruz_after_Titian_-_Charles_V_in_Armour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Pantoja_de_la_Cruz_after_Titian_-_Charles_V_in_Armour.jpg/170px-Pantoja_de_la_Cruz_after_Titian_-_Charles_V_in_Armour.jpg" width="170" height="329" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Pantoja_de_la_Cruz_after_Titian_-_Charles_V_in_Armour.jpg/255px-Pantoja_de_la_Cruz_after_Titian_-_Charles_V_in_Armour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Pantoja_de_la_Cruz_after_Titian_-_Charles_V_in_Armour.jpg/340px-Pantoja_de_la_Cruz_after_Titian_-_Charles_V_in_Armour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="344" data-file-height="666" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pantoja_de_la_Cruz_after_Titian_-_Charles_V_in_Armour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Charles&#160;V with Armor by <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pantoja_de_la_Cruz" title="Juan Pantoja de la Cruz">Juan Pantoja de la Cruz</a> (1605), copying <a href="/wiki/Titian" title="Titian">Titian</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Due to the irregularity of Charles assuming the royal title while his mother, the legitimate queen, was alive, the negotiations with the Castilian <i>Cortes</i> in Valladolid (1518) proved difficult.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> In the end Charles was accepted under the following conditions: he would learn to speak <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Castilian</a>; he would not appoint foreigners; he was prohibited from taking precious metals from Castile; and he would respect the rights of his mother, Queen <a href="/wiki/Joanna_of_Castile" title="Joanna of Castile">Joanna</a>. The Cortes paid homage to him in Valladolid in February 1518. After this, Charles departed to the crown of Aragon. He managed to overcome the resistance of the Aragonese <i>Cortes</i> and Catalan <i>Corts</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> and he was finally recognized as king of Aragon and count of Barcelona jointly with his mother.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre#Spanish_conquest" title="Kingdom of Navarre">Kingdom of Navarre</a> had been <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_Iberian_Navarre" title="Spanish conquest of Iberian Navarre">invaded by Ferdinand of Aragon</a> jointly with Castile in 1512, but he pledged a formal oath to respect the kingdom. On Charles's accession to the Spanish throne, the Parliament of Navarre (<i>Cortes</i>) required him to attend the coronation ceremony (to become Charles IV of Navarre), but this demand fell on deaf ears, and the Parliament kept piling up grievances.</p>
<p>Charles was accepted as sovereign, even though the Spanish felt uneasy with the Imperial style. Spanish kingdoms varied in their traditions. Castile was an authoritarian kingdom, where the monarch's own will easily overrode law and the <i>Cortes</i>. By contrast, in the kingdoms of the crown of Aragon, and especially in the Pyrenean kingdom of Navarre, law prevailed, and the monarchy was <a href="/wiki/Fuero#Basque_and_Pyrenean_fueros" title="Fuero">a contract with the people</a>. This became an inconvenience and a matter of dispute for Charles V and later kings, since realm-specific traditions limited their absolute power. With Charles, government became more absolute, even though until his mother's death in 1555 Charles did not hold the full kingship of the country.</p>
<p>Soon resistance to the Emperor arose because of heavy taxation to support foreign wars in which Castilians had little interest, and because Charles tended to select Flemings for high offices in Spain and America, ignoring Castilian candidates. The resistance culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Revolt_of_the_Comuneros" title="Revolt of the Comuneros">Revolt of the Comuneros</a>, which Charles suppressed. Immediately after crushing the Castilian revolt, Charles was confronted again with the hot issue of Navarre when King <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_Navarre" title="Henry II of Navarre">Henry II</a> attempted to <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_Iberian_Navarre#1521_French-Navarrese_expedition" title="Spanish conquest of Iberian Navarre">reconquer the kingdom</a>. Main military operations lasted until 1524, when <a href="/wiki/Hondarribia" title="Hondarribia">Hondarribia</a> surrendered to Charles's forces, but frequent cross-border clashes in the western Pyrenees only stopped in 1528 (Treaties of Madrid and Cambrai).</p>
<p>After these events, Navarre remained a matter of domestic and international litigation still for a century (a French dynastic claim to the throne did not end until the French Revolution in 1789). Charles wanted his son and heir <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II</a> to marry the heiress of Navarre, <a href="/wiki/Jeanne_d%27Albret" title="Jeanne d'Albret">Jeanne d'Albret</a>. Jeanne was instead forced to marry <a href="/wiki/William,_Duke_of_Julich-Cleves-Berg" class="mw-redirect" title="William, Duke of Julich-Cleves-Berg">William, Duke of Julich-Cleves-Berg</a>, but that childless marriage was annulled after four years. She next married <a href="/wiki/Antoine_de_Bourbon" class="mw-redirect" title="Antoine de Bourbon">Antoine de Bourbon</a>, and both she and their son would oppose <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II</a> in the French Wars of Religion.</p>
<p>Castile became integrated into Charles's empire, and provided the bulk of the empire's financial resources as well as its most effective military units. The enormous budget deficit accumulated during Charles's reign resulted in Spain declaring bankruptcy during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Crown of Aragon</a> inherited by Charles included the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Naples" title="Kingdom of Naples">Kingdom of Naples</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sicily" title="Kingdom of Sicily">Kingdom of Sicily</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sardinia#Modern_history" title="Sardinia">Kingdom of Sardinia</a>. Aragon also previously controlled the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Milan" title="Duchy of Milan">Duchy of Milan</a>, but a year before Charles ascended to the throne, it was annexed by <a href="/wiki/Early_Modern_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Early Modern France">France</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Marignano" title="Battle of Marignano">Battle of Marignano</a> in 1515. Charles succeeded in re-capturing Milan in 1522, when Imperial troops defeated the Franco-Swiss army at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bicocca" title="Battle of Bicocca">Bicocca</a>. Yet in 1524 Francis I of France retook the initiative, crossing into Lombardy where Milan, along with a number of other cities, once again fell to his attack. <a href="/wiki/Pavia" title="Pavia">Pavia</a> alone held out, and on 24 February 1525 (Charles's twenty-fifth birthday), Charles's <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Army" title="Spanish Army">Spanish</a> forces captured Francis and crushed his army in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pavia" title="Battle of Pavia">Battle of Pavia</a>, yet again retaking Milan and Lombardy. Spain successfully held on to all of its Italian territories, though they were invaded again on multiple occasions during the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Wars" title="Italian Wars">Italian Wars</a>.</p>
<p>In addition, Habsburg trade in the Mediterranean was consistently disrupted by the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. In 1538 a <a href="/wiki/Holy_League_(1538)" title="Holy League (1538)">Holy League</a> consisting of all the Italian states and Spain was formed to drive the Ottomans back, but it was defeated at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Preveza_(1538)" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Preveza (1538)">Battle of Preveza</a>. Decisive naval victory eluded Charles; it would not be achieved until after Charles's death, at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto" title="Battle of Lepanto">Battle of Lepanto</a> in 1571.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="America">America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During Charles's reign, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish territories in the Americas</a> were considerably extended by <i><a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistadores</a></i> like <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hernán Cortés">Hernán Cortés</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Pizarro" title="Francisco Pizarro">Francisco Pizarro</a>. They conquered the large <a href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">Aztec</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inca" class="mw-redirect" title="Inca">Inca</a> empires and incorporated them into the Empire as the Viceroyalties of <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_Peru" title="Viceroyalty of Peru">Peru</a> between 1519 and 1542. Combined with the circumnavigation of the globe by the <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Magellan%27s_circumnavigation" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of Magellan's circumnavigation">Magellan expedition</a> in 1522, these successes convinced Charles of his divine mission to become the leader of <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">Christendom</a>, which still perceived a significant threat from Islam. The conquests also helped solidify Charles's rule by providing the state treasury with enormous amounts of <a href="/wiki/Bullion" title="Bullion">bullion</a>. As the conquistador <a href="/wiki/Bernal_D%C3%ADaz_del_Castillo" title="Bernal Díaz del Castillo">Bernal Díaz del Castillo</a> observed, "We came to serve God and his Majesty, to give light to those in darkness, and also to acquire that wealth which most men covet."<sup id="cite_ref-Prescott_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prescott-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1528 Charles assigned a concession in <a href="/wiki/Venezuela_Province" title="Venezuela Province">Venezuela Province</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bartholomeus_V._Welser" title="Bartholomeus V. Welser">Bartholomeus V. Welser</a>, in compensation for his inability to repay debts owed. The concession, known as <a href="/wiki/Klein-Venedig" title="Klein-Venedig">Klein-Venedig</a> (<i>little Venice</i>), was revoked in 1546. In 1550, Charles convened a conference at <a href="/wiki/Valladolid" title="Valladolid">Valladolid</a> in order to <a href="/wiki/Valladolid_debate" title="Valladolid debate">consider the morality of the force</a> used against the indigenous populations of the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>, which included figures such as <a href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_de_las_Casas" title="Bartolomé de las Casas">Bartolomé de las Casas</a>.</p>
<p>Charles V is credited with the first idea of constructing an American Isthmus canal in Panama as early as 1520.<sup id="cite_ref-Haskin_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haskin-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Holy_Roman_Empire">Holy Roman Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Holy Roman Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Papa_Clemente_VII_e_l%27imperatore_Carlo_V_a_cavallo_sotto_un_baldacchino_(8_de_agosto_de_2018,_Museo_degli_affreschi_Giovanni_Battista_Cavalcaselle,_Verona).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Papa_Clemente_VII_e_l%27imperatore_Carlo_V_a_cavallo_sotto_un_baldacchino_%288_de_agosto_de_2018%2C_Museo_degli_affreschi_Giovanni_Battista_Cavalcaselle%2C_Verona%29.jpg/270px-Papa_Clemente_VII_e_l%27imperatore_Carlo_V_a_cavallo_sotto_un_baldacchino_%288_de_agosto_de_2018%2C_Museo_degli_affreschi_Giovanni_Battista_Cavalcaselle%2C_Verona%29.jpg" width="270" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Papa_Clemente_VII_e_l%27imperatore_Carlo_V_a_cavallo_sotto_un_baldacchino_%288_de_agosto_de_2018%2C_Museo_degli_affreschi_Giovanni_Battista_Cavalcaselle%2C_Verona%29.jpg/405px-Papa_Clemente_VII_e_l%27imperatore_Carlo_V_a_cavallo_sotto_un_baldacchino_%288_de_agosto_de_2018%2C_Museo_degli_affreschi_Giovanni_Battista_Cavalcaselle%2C_Verona%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Papa_Clemente_VII_e_l%27imperatore_Carlo_V_a_cavallo_sotto_un_baldacchino_%288_de_agosto_de_2018%2C_Museo_degli_affreschi_Giovanni_Battista_Cavalcaselle%2C_Verona%29.jpg/540px-Papa_Clemente_VII_e_l%27imperatore_Carlo_V_a_cavallo_sotto_un_baldacchino_%288_de_agosto_de_2018%2C_Museo_degli_affreschi_Giovanni_Battista_Cavalcaselle%2C_Verona%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3134" data-file-height="1942" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Papa_Clemente_VII_e_l%27imperatore_Carlo_V_a_cavallo_sotto_un_baldacchino_(8_de_agosto_de_2018,_Museo_degli_affreschi_Giovanni_Battista_Cavalcaselle,_Verona).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Pope Clement VII and Emperor Charles V on horseback under a canopy</i>, by <a href="/wiki/Jacopo_Ligozzi" title="Jacopo Ligozzi">Jacopo Ligozzi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Circa" title="Circa">c.</a> 1580. It describes the entry of the Pope and the Emperor into Bologna in 1530, when the latter was crowned as Holy Roman Emperor by the former.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the death of his paternal grandfather, <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Maximilian I, Holy Roman Emperor">Maximilian</a>, in 1519, Charles inherited the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg Monarchy</a>. He was also the natural candidate of the <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">electors</a> to succeed his grandfather as Holy Roman Emperor. He defeated the candidacies of <a href="/wiki/Frederick_III,_Elector_of_Saxony" title="Frederick III, Elector of Saxony">Frederick III, Elector of Saxony</a>, Francis I of France, and <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII of England</a>. The electors gave Charles the crown on 28 June 1519. On 26 October 1520 he was crowned in Germany and some ten years later, on 22 February 1530, he was crowned <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a> by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_VII" title="Pope Clement VII">Pope Clement VII</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bologna" title="Bologna">Bologna</a>, the last emperor to receive a papal coronation.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite holding the imperial throne, Charles's real authority was limited by the German princes. They gained a strong foothold in the Empire's territories, and Charles was determined not to let this happen in the Netherlands. An <a href="/wiki/Inquisition" title="Inquisition">inquisition</a> was established as early as 1522. In 1550, the death penalty was introduced for all cases of unrepentant heresy. Political dissent was also firmly controlled, most notably in his place of birth, where Charles, assisted by the <a href="/wiki/Fernando_%C3%81lvarez_de_Toledo,_3rd_Duke_of_Alba" title="Fernando Álvarez de Toledo, 3rd Duke of Alba">Duke of Alba</a>, personally suppressed the <a href="/wiki/Revolt_of_Ghent_(1539)" title="Revolt of Ghent (1539)">Revolt of Ghent</a> in mid-February 1540.<sup id="cite_ref-Kamen_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kamen-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Charles abdicated as emperor in 1556 in favor of his brother Ferdinand; however, due to lengthy debate and bureaucratic procedure, the Imperial Diet did not accept the abdication (and thus make it legally valid) until 24 February 1558. Up to that date, Charles continued to use the title of emperor.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Truce_of_Nice_1538.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Truce_of_Nice_1538.jpg/220px-Truce_of_Nice_1538.jpg" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Truce_of_Nice_1538.jpg/330px-Truce_of_Nice_1538.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Truce_of_Nice_1538.jpg/440px-Truce_of_Nice_1538.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2016" data-file-height="1543" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Truce_of_Nice_1538.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Francis I and Charles V made peace at the <a href="/wiki/Truce_of_Nice" class="mw-redirect" title="Truce of Nice">Truce of Nice</a> in 1538. Francis actually refused to meet Charles in person, and the treaty was signed in separate rooms.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Much of Charles's reign was taken up by conflicts with France, which found itself encircled by Charles's empire while it still maintained ambitions in Italy. In 1520, Charles visited <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, where his aunt, <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Aragon" title="Catherine of Aragon">Catherine of Aragon</a>, urged her husband, Henry VIII, to ally himself with the emperor. In 1508 Charles was nominated by Henry VII to the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Garter" title="Order of the Garter">Order of the Garter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> His <a href="/wiki/Garter_stall_plate" title="Garter stall plate">Garter stall plate</a> survives in <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Chapel,_Windsor_Castle" title="St George's Chapel, Windsor Castle">Saint George's Chapel</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Italian_War_of_1521" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian War of 1521">first war</a> with Charles's great nemesis <a href="/wiki/Francis_I_of_France" title="Francis I of France">Francis I of France</a> began in 1521. Charles allied with England and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_X" title="Pope Leo X">Pope Leo X</a> against the French and the Venetians, and was highly successful, driving the French out of <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> and defeating and capturing Francis at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pavia" title="Battle of Pavia">Battle of Pavia</a> in 1525. To gain his freedom, Francis ceded <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Burgundy" title="Duchy of Burgundy">Burgundy</a> to Charles in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Madrid_(1526)" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Madrid (1526)">Treaty of Madrid</a>, as well as renouncing his support of Henry II's claim over <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">Navarre</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Karl_V.-Carlos_I._1548_(Tiziano_Vecellio%3F)_066.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Karl_V.-Carlos_I._1548_%28Tiziano_Vecellio%3F%29_066.jpg/220px-Karl_V.-Carlos_I._1548_%28Tiziano_Vecellio%3F%29_066.jpg" width="220" height="379" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Karl_V.-Carlos_I._1548_%28Tiziano_Vecellio%3F%29_066.jpg/330px-Karl_V.-Carlos_I._1548_%28Tiziano_Vecellio%3F%29_066.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Karl_V.-Carlos_I._1548_%28Tiziano_Vecellio%3F%29_066.jpg/440px-Karl_V.-Carlos_I._1548_%28Tiziano_Vecellio%3F%29_066.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1576" data-file-height="2718" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Karl_V.-Carlos_I._1548_(Tiziano_Vecellio%3F)_066.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Portrait, 1548, by <a href="/wiki/Lambert_Sustris" title="Lambert Sustris">Lambert Sustris</a> (formerly attributed to <a href="/wiki/Titian" title="Titian">Titian</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>When he was released, however, Francis had the Parliament of Paris denounce the treaty because it had been signed under <a href="/wiki/Duress" class="mw-redirect" title="Duress">duress</a>. France then joined the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_League_of_Cognac" title="War of the League of Cognac">League of Cognac</a> that <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_VII" title="Pope Clement VII">Pope Clement VII</a> had formed with Henry VIII of England, the Venetians, the Florentines, and the Milanese to resist imperial domination of Italy. In the ensuing war, Charles's <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Rome_(1527)" title="Sack of Rome (1527)">sack of Rome (1527)</a> and virtual imprisonment of Pope Clement VII in 1527 prevented the Pope from <a href="/wiki/Annulment_(Catholic_Church)" class="mw-redirect" title="Annulment (Catholic Church)">annulling</a> the marriage of Henry VIII of England and Charles's aunt <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Aragon" title="Catherine of Aragon">Catherine of Aragon</a>, so Henry eventually broke with Rome, thus leading to the <a href="/wiki/English_Reformation" title="English Reformation">English Reformation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Holmes1993a_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmes1993a-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Froude1891a_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Froude1891a-36">[36]</a></sup> In other respects, the war was inconclusive. In the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Cambrai" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Cambrai">Treaty of Cambrai</a> (1529), called the "Ladies' Peace" because it was negotiated between Charles's aunt and Francis' mother, Francis renounced his claims in Italy but retained control of Burgundy.</p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Italian_War_of_1536%E2%80%9338" title="Italian War of 1536–38">third war</a> erupted in 1536. Following the death of <a href="/wiki/Francesco_II_Sforza" title="Francesco II Sforza">the last Sforza Duke of Milan</a>, Charles installed his son <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip</a> in the duchy, despite Francis's claims on it. This war too was inconclusive. Francis failed to conquer Milan, but he succeeded in conquering most of the lands of Charles's ally, the <a href="/wiki/Charles_III,_Duke_of_Savoy" title="Charles III, Duke of Savoy">Duke of Savoy</a>, including his capital <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a>. A truce at <a href="/wiki/Nice" title="Nice">Nice</a> in 1538 on the basis of <i><a href="/wiki/Uti_possidetis" title="Uti possidetis">uti possidetis</a></i> ended the war but lasted only a short time. <a href="/wiki/Italian_War_of_1542%E2%80%9346" title="Italian War of 1542–46">War resumed in 1542</a>, with Francis now allied with Ottoman Sultan <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman I</a> and Charles once again allied with Henry VIII. Despite the conquest of Nice by a <a href="/wiki/Franco-Ottoman_alliance" title="Franco-Ottoman alliance">Franco-Ottoman fleet</a>, the French could not advance toward Milan, while a joint Anglo-Imperial invasion of northern France, led by Charles himself, won some successes but was ultimately abandoned, leading to another peace and restoration of the <i>status quo ante bellum</i> in 1544.</p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Italian_War_of_1551%E2%80%931559" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian War of 1551–1559">final war</a> erupted with Francis' son and successor, <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_France" title="Henry II of France">Henry II</a>, in 1551. Henry won early success in <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Lorraine" title="Duchy of Lorraine">Lorraine</a>, where he captured <a href="/wiki/Metz" title="Metz">Metz</a>, but French offensives in Italy failed. Charles abdicated midway through this conflict, leaving further conduct of the war to his son, <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II</a>, and his brother, <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Ferdinand I, Holy Roman Emperor">Ferdinand I, Holy Roman Emperor</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conflicts_with_the_Ottoman_Empire">Conflicts with the Ottoman Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Conflicts with the Ottoman Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_and_Islam" title="Protestantism and Islam">Protestantism and Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Habsburg-Persian_alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg-Persian alliance">Habsburg-Persian alliance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_Tunis_(1534)" title="Conquest of Tunis (1534)">Conquest of Tunis (1534)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_Tunis_(1535)" title="Conquest of Tunis (1535)">conquest of Tunis (1535)</a></div>
<p>Charles fought continually with the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and its sultan, <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman the Magnificent</a>. The defeat of Hungary at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs" title="Battle of Mohács">Battle of Mohács</a> in 1526 "sent a wave of terror over Europe."<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The Muslim advance in Central Europe was halted at the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Vienna" title="Siege of Vienna">Siege of Vienna</a> in 1529.</p>
<p>Suleiman won the contest for mastery of the Mediterranean, in spite of Spanish victories such as the <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_Tunis_(1535)" title="Conquest of Tunis (1535)">conquest of Tunis</a> in 1535. The regular Ottoman fleet came to dominate the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean" title="Eastern Mediterranean">Eastern Mediterranean</a> after its victories at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Preveza" title="Battle of Preveza">Preveza</a> in 1538 and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Djerba" title="Battle of Djerba">Djerba</a> in 1560 (shortly after Charles's death), which severely decimated the Spanish marine arm. At the same time, the Muslim <a href="/wiki/Barbary_corsairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbary corsairs">Barbary corsairs</a>, acting under the general authority and supervision of the sultan, regularly devastated the Spanish and Italian coasts, crippling Spanish trade and chipping at the foundations of Habsburg power.</p>
<p>In 1536 <a href="/wiki/Francis_I_of_France" title="Francis I of France">Francis I of France</a> allied himself with Suleiman against Charles. While Francis was persuaded to sign a peace treaty in 1538, he again allied himself with the Ottomans in 1542 in a <a href="/wiki/Franco-Ottoman_alliance" title="Franco-Ottoman alliance">Franco-Ottoman alliance</a>. In 1543 Charles allied himself with Henry VIII and forced Francis to sign the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Cr%C3%A9py" class="mw-redirect" title="Peace of Crépy">Truce of Crépy-en-Laonnois</a>. Later, in 1547, Charles signed a humiliating<sup id="cite_ref-treaty_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-treaty-39">[39]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Truce_of_Adrianople_(1547)" title="Truce of Adrianople (1547)">treaty</a> with the Ottomans to gain himself some respite from the huge expenses of their war.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Charles V made overtures to the <a href="/wiki/Safavid_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Safavid Empire">Safavid Empire</a> to open a second front against the Ottomans, in an attempt at creating a <a href="/wiki/Habsburg-Persian_alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg-Persian alliance">Habsburg-Persian alliance</a>. Contacts were positive, but rendered difficult by enormous distances. In effect, however, the Safavids did enter in conflict with the Ottoman Empire in the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman-Safavid_War_(1532%E2%80%931555)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman-Safavid War (1532–1555)">Ottoman-Safavid War</a>, forcing it to split its military resources.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Protestant_Reformation">Protestant Reformation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Protestant Reformation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carlos_V_en_M%C3%BChlberg,_by_Titian,_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Carlos_V_en_M%C3%BChlberg%2C_by_Titian%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg/220px-Carlos_V_en_M%C3%BChlberg%2C_by_Titian%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg" width="220" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Carlos_V_en_M%C3%BChlberg%2C_by_Titian%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg/330px-Carlos_V_en_M%C3%BChlberg%2C_by_Titian%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Carlos_V_en_M%C3%BChlberg%2C_by_Titian%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg/440px-Carlos_V_en_M%C3%BChlberg%2C_by_Titian%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg 2x" data-file-width="25284" data-file-height="30000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carlos_V_en_M%C3%BChlberg,_by_Titian,_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Charles&#160;V on horseback in Mühlberg. <a href="/wiki/Titian" title="Titian">Titian</a>, 1548, <a href="/wiki/Museo_del_Prado" title="Museo del Prado">Museo del Prado</a>, Madrid, Spain</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>, Charles called <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Diet_of_Worms" title="Diet of Worms">Diet of Worms</a> in 1521, promising him safe conduct if he would appear. Initially dismissing Luther's <a href="/wiki/The_Ninety-Five_Theses" class="mw-redirect" title="The Ninety-Five Theses">theses</a> as "an argument between monks", he later outlawed Luther and his followers in that same year but was tied up with other concerns and unable to take action against Protestantism. The <a href="/wiki/German_Peasants%27_War" title="German Peasants' War">Peasants' Revolt</a> in Germany broke out from 1524 to 1526, and in 1531 the Lutheran <a href="/wiki/Schmalkaldic_League" title="Schmalkaldic League">Schmalkaldic League</a> was formed. Charles delegated increasing responsibility for Germany to his brother <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Ferdinand I, Holy Roman Emperor">Ferdinand</a> while he concentrated on problems elsewhere.</p>
<p>In 1545, the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Trent" title="Council of Trent">Council of Trent</a> began the <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">Counter-Reformation</a>, and Charles won to the Catholic cause some of the princes of the Holy Roman Empire<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. In 1546 (the year of Luther's natural death), he outlawed the Schmalkaldic League (which had occupied the territory of another prince). The next year his forces drove the League's troops out of southern Germany, and defeated <a href="/wiki/John_Frederick,_Elector_of_Saxony" class="mw-redirect" title="John Frederick, Elector of Saxony">John Frederick, Elector of Saxony</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philip_I_of_Hesse" class="mw-redirect" title="Philip I of Hesse">Philip of Hesse</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_M%C3%BChlberg" title="Battle of Mühlberg">Battle of Mühlberg</a>, capturing both. At the <a href="/wiki/Augsburg_Interim" title="Augsburg Interim">Augsburg Interim</a> in 1548, he created a solution giving certain allowances to Protestants until the Council of Trent would restore unity. However, members of both sides resented the Interim and some actively opposed it. In 1552 Protestant princes, in alliance with <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_France" title="Henry II of France">Henry II of France</a>, rebelled again, which caused Charles to retreat to the Netherlands.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage">Marriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Marriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>During his lifetime, Charles had several mistresses, but only during his bachelorhood and only once during his widowhood; there are no records of him ever having had any extramarital affairs during his marriage.</p>
<p>Negotiations for Charles's marriage first began shortly after his arrival in Spain, with the Spanish nobles expressing their wishes for him to marry his first cousin the Infanta <a href="/wiki/Isabella_of_Portugal" title="Isabella of Portugal">Isabella of Portugal</a>, daughter of King <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Manuel I of Portugal">Manuel I of Portugal</a> and Queen <a href="/wiki/Maria_of_Aragon,_Queen_of_Portugal" title="Maria of Aragon, Queen of Portugal">Maria of Aragon</a> and sister of King <a href="/wiki/John_III_of_Portugal" title="John III of Portugal">John III of Portugal</a>. The nobles desired for Charles to marry a princess of Spanish blood and a marriage to Isabella would secure an alliance between Spain and Portugal. The 18 year old king, however, ignored the nobles' advice and, instead of marrying Isabella, he sent his sister <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_of_Austria" title="Eleanor of Austria">Eleanor of Austria</a> to marry Isabella's widowed father King Manuel. In 1521, on the advice of his Flemish advisors, Charles became engaged to his other first cousin <a href="/wiki/Mary_I_of_England" title="Mary I of England">Mary Tudor</a>, daughter of his aunt <a href="/wiki/Katherine_of_Aragon" class="mw-redirect" title="Katherine of Aragon">Katherine of Aragon</a> and King <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII of England</a> in order to secure an alliance with England. However, this engagement was very problematic; Mary Tudor was only 6 years old at the time, sixteen years Charles's junior, which meant that Charles would have to wait for her to be old enough to marry.</p>
<p>By 1525, Charles was no longer interested in an alliance with England and was determined to have legitimate children and heirs. He abandoned idea of an alliance with England, cancelled his engagement to Mary Tudor and decided to marry Isabella and form an alliance with Portugal. Charles wrote to King John, making a double marriage contract - Charles would marry Isabella and John would marry Charles's youngest sister <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Austria,_Queen_of_Portugal" title="Catherine of Austria, Queen of Portugal">Catherine of Austria</a>. A marriage to Isabella was more beneficiary for Charles, as she was closer to him in age and provided him with a very handsome dowry of 900,000 Portuguese cruzados or Castilian folds that would solve his financial problems brought on by the Italian Wars.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Charles_V_and_Empress_Isabella_of_Portugal,_by_Peter_Paul_Rubens.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Charles_V_and_Empress_Isabella_of_Portugal%2C_by_Peter_Paul_Rubens.jpg/220px-Charles_V_and_Empress_Isabella_of_Portugal%2C_by_Peter_Paul_Rubens.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Charles_V_and_Empress_Isabella_of_Portugal%2C_by_Peter_Paul_Rubens.jpg/330px-Charles_V_and_Empress_Isabella_of_Portugal%2C_by_Peter_Paul_Rubens.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Charles_V_and_Empress_Isabella_of_Portugal%2C_by_Peter_Paul_Rubens.jpg/440px-Charles_V_and_Empress_Isabella_of_Portugal%2C_by_Peter_Paul_Rubens.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2395" data-file-height="1697" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Charles_V_and_Empress_Isabella_of_Portugal,_by_Peter_Paul_Rubens.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Emperor Charles V and Empress Isabella. <a href="/wiki/Peter_Paul_Rubens" title="Peter Paul Rubens">Peter Paul Rubens</a> after <a href="/wiki/Titian" title="Titian">Titian</a>, 17th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 11 March 1526, Charles and Isabella were married at the <a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Seville" title="Alcázar of Seville">Alcázar Palace</a> in <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>. The marriage was originally a political arrangement, but on their first meeting, the couple fell deeply in love, with Isabella captivating the Emperor with her beauty and charm. Following their wedding, Charles and Isabella spent a long and happy honeymoon at the <a href="/wiki/Alhambra" title="Alhambra">Alhambra</a> in <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">Granada</a>. Despite the Emperor's long absences due to political affairs abroad, the marriage was a happy one, as both partners were always devoted and faithful to each other.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The Empress would act as regent of Spain during her husband's absences and she proved herself to be a good politician and ruler.</p>
<p>The marriage lasted for thirteen years, until Isabella died in childbirth at the age of 35 on 1 May 1539 after giving birth to a stillborn son. The Emperor was left so grief-stricken by his wife's death that he shut himself up in a monastery for two months where he would pray and mourn for her.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In the aftermath, Charles never recovered from the loss; he dressed in black for the rest of his life and, unlike most kings of the time, he never remarried. In memory of his wife, Charles commissioned the painter <a href="/wiki/Titian" title="Titian">Titian</a> to paint several posthumous portraits of Isabella; the portraits that were produced included Titian's <i><a href="/wiki/Portrait_of_Isabella_of_Portugal" title="Portrait of Isabella of Portugal">Portrait of Empress Isabel of Portugal</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/La_Gloria_(Titian)" title="La Gloria (Titian)">La Gloria</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Charles kept these portraits with him whenever he travelled and they were among those that he brought with him to the Monastery of Yuste after his retirement.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Charles also paid tribute to Isabella's memory with music when, in 1540, he commissioned the Flemish composer <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Crecquillon" title="Thomas Crecquillon">Thomas Crecquillon</a> to compose new music as a memorial to her. Crecquillon composed his <i>Missa 'Mort m'a privé'</i> in memory of the Empress, which, itself, expresses the Emperor's grief and great wish for a heavenly reunion with his beloved wife.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Charles suffered from an enlarged <a href="/wiki/Human_lower_jaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Human lower jaw">lower jaw</a>, a deformity that became considerably worse in later Habsburg generations, giving rise to the term <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_jaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg jaw">Habsburg jaw</a>. This deformity may have been caused by the family's long history of inbreeding, which was commonly practiced in royal families of that era to maintain dynastic control of territory.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> He suffered from <a href="/wiki/Epilepsy" title="Epilepsy">epilepsy</a><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> and was seriously afflicted with <a href="/wiki/Gout" title="Gout">gout</a>, presumably caused by a diet consisting mainly of <a href="/wiki/Red_meat" title="Red meat">red meat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> As he aged, his gout progressed from painful to crippling. In his retirement, he was carried around the monastery of <a href="/wiki/Yuste" class="mw-redirect" title="Yuste">St. Yuste</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Litter_(vehicle)" title="Litter (vehicle)">sedan chair</a>. A ramp was specially constructed to allow him easy access to his rooms.<sup id="cite_ref-Rady_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rady-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Abdications_and_later_life">Abdications and later life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Abdications and later life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Busto_de_Carlos_V.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Busto_de_Carlos_V.jpg/220px-Busto_de_Carlos_V.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Busto_de_Carlos_V.jpg/330px-Busto_de_Carlos_V.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Busto_de_Carlos_V.jpg/440px-Busto_de_Carlos_V.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Busto_de_Carlos_V.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bronze bust, by <a href="/wiki/Leone_Leoni" title="Leone Leoni">Leone Leoni</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Pompeo_Leoni" class="mw-redirect" title="Pompeo Leoni">Pompeo Leoni</a>, 1553</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Charles abdicated the parts of his empire piecemeal. First he abdicated the thrones of Sicily and Naples, both fiefs of the Papacy, and the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Milan" title="Duchy of Milan">Duchy of Milan</a> to his son <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip</a> in 1554. Upon Charles's abdication of Naples on 25 July, Philip was invested with the kingdom (officially "Naples and Sicily") on 2 October by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Julius_III" title="Pope Julius III">Pope Julius III</a>. The abdication of the throne of Sicily, sometimes dated to 16 January 1556, must have taken place before Joanna's death in 1555. There is a record of Philip being invested with this kingdom (officially "Sicily and Jerusalem") on 18 November 1554 by Julius. These resignations are confirmed in Charles's will from the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-Braudel_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Braudel-50">[50]</a></sup> The most famous—and public—abdication of Charles took place a year later, on 25 October 1555, when he announced to the <a href="/wiki/States_General_of_the_Netherlands" title="States General of the Netherlands">States General of the Netherlands</a> his abdication of those territories and the county of Charolais and his intention to retire to a monastery.<sup id="cite_ref-Braudel_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Braudel-50">[50]</a></sup> He abdicated as ruler of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> in January 1556, with no fanfare, and gave these possessions to Philip.<sup id="cite_ref-Braudel_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Braudel-50">[50]</a></sup> In September 1556, he abdicated as Holy Roman Emperor in favor of his brother Ferdinand, although the abdication was not formally accepted by the <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">Electors of the Empire</a> until 1558.<sup id="cite_ref-Whaley2012_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whaley2012-51">[51]</a></sup> The delay had been at the request of Ferdinand, who had been concerned about holding a risky election in 1556.<sup id="cite_ref-Braudel_50-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Braudel-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Charles retired to the Monastery of <a href="/wiki/Yuste" class="mw-redirect" title="Yuste">Yuste</a> in Extremadura but continued to correspond widely and kept an interest in the situation of the empire. He suffered from severe <a href="/wiki/Gout" title="Gout">gout</a>. Some scholars think Charles decided to abdicate after a gout attack in 1552 forced him to postpone an attempt to recapture the city of Metz, where he was later defeated. He lived alone in a secluded monastery, with clocks lining every wall, which some historians believe were symbols of his reign and his lack of time.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Escorial_Basilica,_bronze_effigy_of_Emperor_Charles_V_and_Empress_Isabella.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/83/El_Escorial_Basilica%2C_bronze_effigy_of_Emperor_Charles_V_and_Empress_Isabella.jpg/220px-El_Escorial_Basilica%2C_bronze_effigy_of_Emperor_Charles_V_and_Empress_Isabella.jpg" width="220" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/83/El_Escorial_Basilica%2C_bronze_effigy_of_Emperor_Charles_V_and_Empress_Isabella.jpg/330px-El_Escorial_Basilica%2C_bronze_effigy_of_Emperor_Charles_V_and_Empress_Isabella.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/83/El_Escorial_Basilica%2C_bronze_effigy_of_Emperor_Charles_V_and_Empress_Isabella.jpg/440px-El_Escorial_Basilica%2C_bronze_effigy_of_Emperor_Charles_V_and_Empress_Isabella.jpg 2x" data-file-width="819" data-file-height="758" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Escorial_Basilica,_bronze_effigy_of_Emperor_Charles_V_and_Empress_Isabella.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The bronze effigies of Charles and Isabella at the Basilica in El Escorial</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In August 1558, Charles was taken seriously ill with what was later revealed to be <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> He died in the early hours of the morning on 21st September 1558, at the age of 58, holding in his hand the cross that his wife Isabella had been holding when she died.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Charles was originally buried in the chapel of the Monastery of Yuste, but he left a <a href="/wiki/Codicil_(will)" title="Codicil (will)">codicil</a> in his last will and testament asking for the establishment of a new religious foundation in which he would be reburied with Isabella.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Following his return to Spain in 1559, their son Philip undertook the task of fulfilling his father's wish when he founded the <a href="/wiki/El_Escorial" title="El Escorial">Monastery of San Lorenzo de El Escorial</a>. After the Monastery's Royal Crypt was completed in 1574, the bodies of Charles and Isabella were relocated and re-interred into a small vault directly underneath the altar of the famous Basilica of the Monastery, in accordance with Charles's wishes to be buried "half-body under the altar and half-body under the priest's feet" side by side with Isabella. They remained in this vault until 1654 when they were later moved into the Royal Pantheon of Kings by their great-grandson <a href="/wiki/Philip_IV_of_Spain" title="Philip IV of Spain">Philip IV</a>, who, in doing so, disrespected his great-grandfather's wishes.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>On one side of the Basilica are bronze effigies of Charles and Isabella, with effigies of their daughter <a href="/wiki/Maria_of_Austria,_Holy_Roman_Empress" title="Maria of Austria, Holy Roman Empress">Maria of Austria</a> and Charles's sisters <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_of_Austria" title="Eleanor of Austria">Eleanor of Austria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mary_of_Hungary_(governor_of_the_Netherlands)" title="Mary of Hungary (governor of the Netherlands)">Maria of Hungary</a> behind them. Exactly adjacent to them on the opposite side of the Basilica are effigies of their son Philip with three of his wives and their ill-fated grandson <a href="/wiki/Carlos,_Prince_of_Asturias" title="Carlos, Prince of Asturias">Carlos, Prince of Asturias</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Issue">Issue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Issue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Charles and Isabella had six children, though only three survived to adulthood:</p>

<tr>
<td><b>Son</b><br /></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Greater_Coat_of_Arms_of_Charles_I_of_Spain,_Charles_V_as_Holy_Roman_Emperor_(1530-1556).svg" class="image"><img alt="Greater Coat of Arms of Charles I of Spain, Charles V as Holy Roman Emperor (1530-1556).svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Greater_Coat_of_Arms_of_Charles_I_of_Spain%2C_Charles_V_as_Holy_Roman_Emperor_%281530-1556%29.svg/120px-Greater_Coat_of_Arms_of_Charles_I_of_Spain%2C_Charles_V_as_Holy_Roman_Emperor_%281530-1556%29.svg.png" width="120" height="126" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Greater_Coat_of_Arms_of_Charles_I_of_Spain%2C_Charles_V_as_Holy_Roman_Emperor_%281530-1556%29.svg/180px-Greater_Coat_of_Arms_of_Charles_I_of_Spain%2C_Charles_V_as_Holy_Roman_Emperor_%281530-1556%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Greater_Coat_of_Arms_of_Charles_I_of_Spain%2C_Charles_V_as_Holy_Roman_Emperor_%281530-1556%29.svg/240px-Greater_Coat_of_Arms_of_Charles_I_of_Spain%2C_Charles_V_as_Holy_Roman_Emperor_%281530-1556%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1255" data-file-height="1314" /></a></td>
<td>21 April 1539</td>
<td>Stillborn.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Due to Philip II being a grandson of <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Manuel I of Portugal">Manuel I of Portugal</a> through his mother he was in the line of succession to the throne of Portugal, and claimed it after his uncle's death (<a href="/wiki/Henry_I_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry I of Portugal">Henry, the Cardinal-King</a>, in 1580), thus establishing the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a>.</p>
<p>Charles also had four illegitimate children:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Margaret_of_Parma" title="Margaret of Parma">Margaret of Austria</a> (1522 – 1586), daughter of <a href="/wiki/Johanna_Maria_van_der_Gheynst" title="Johanna Maria van der Gheynst">Johanna Maria van der Gheynst</a>, a servant of <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_de_Lalaing" title="Charles I de Lalaing">Charles I de Lalaing</a>, Seigneur de Montigny, daughter of Gilles Johann van der Gheynst and wife Johanna van der Caye van Cocamby. Married firstly with <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_de%27_Medici,_Duke_of_Florence" title="Alessandro de' Medici, Duke of Florence">Alessandro de' Medici, Duke of Florence</a> and secondly with <a href="/wiki/Ottavio_Farnese,_Duke_of_Parma" title="Ottavio Farnese, Duke of Parma">Ottavio Farnese, Duke of Parma</a>.</li>
<li>Joanna of Austria (1522 – 1530), daughter of a noble lady from Nassau.</li>
<li>Tadea of Austria (1523? – ca. 1562), daughter of Orsolina della Penna. Married with Sinibaldo di Copeschi.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_of_Austria" title="John of Austria">John of Austria</a> (1547 – 1578), son of <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Blomberg" title="Barbara Blomberg">Barbara Blomberg</a>, victor of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto" title="Battle of Lepanto">Battle of Lepanto</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Historians suspect he fathered Isabel of Castile, the illegitimate daughter of his step-grandmother <a href="/wiki/Germaine_of_Foix" title="Germaine of Foix">Germaine of Foix</a>.</p>

<td><a href="/wiki/File:Austria_coat_of_arms_simple.svg" class="image"><img alt="Austria coat of arms simple.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Austria_coat_of_arms_simple.svg/40px-Austria_coat_of_arms_simple.svg.png" width="40" height="44" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Austria_coat_of_arms_simple.svg/60px-Austria_coat_of_arms_simple.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Austria_coat_of_arms_simple.svg/80px-Austria_coat_of_arms_simple.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="275" data-file-height="300" /></a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Austria" title="List of rulers of Austria">Archduke of Austria</a></td>
<td>12 January 1519</td>
<td>12 January 1521</td>
<td>Charles I</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The titles of King of Hungary, of Bohemia, and of Croatia, were incorporated into the imperial family during Charles's reign, but they were held, both nominally and substantively, by his brother Ferdinand, who initiated a four-century-long Habsburg rule over these eastern territories.</p>
<p>However, according Charles V testament, the titles of King of Hungary, of Dalmatia, and of Croatia and others were legated to his grandson, Infante <a href="/wiki/Carlos,_Prince_of_Asturias" title="Carlos, Prince of Asturias">Carlos, Prince of Asturias</a> who was the son of <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II of Spain</a>, and who died young. Charles's full titulature went as follows:</p>
<p><i>Charles, <a href="/wiki/By_the_grace_of_God" class="mw-redirect" title="By the grace of God">by the grace of God</a>, Holy Roman Emperor, forever <a href="/wiki/Augustus_(honorific)" title="Augustus (honorific)">August</a>, King of Germany, King of Italy, King of all Spains, of Castile, Aragon, León, of Hungary, of Dalmatia, of Croatia, Navarra, Grenada, Toledo, Valencia, Galicia, Majorca, Sevilla, Cordova, Murcia, Jaén, Algarves, Algeciras, Gibraltar, the Canary Islands, King of Two Sicilies, of Sardinia, Corsica, King of Jerusalem, King of the Western and Eastern Indies, of the Islands and Mainland of the Ocean Sea, Archduke of Austria, Duke of Burgundy, Brabant, Lorraine, Styria, Carinthia, Carniola, Limburg, Luxembourg, Gelderland, Neopatria, Württemberg, Landgrave of Alsace, Prince of Swabia, Asturia and Catalonia, Count of Flanders, Habsburg, Tyrol, Gorizia, Barcelona, Artois, Burgundy Palatine, Hainaut, Holland, Seeland, Ferrette, Kyburg, Namur, Roussillon, Cerdagne, Drenthe, Zutphen, Margrave of the Holy Roman Empire, Burgau, <a href="/wiki/Oristano" title="Oristano">Oristano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gociano" class="mw-redirect" title="Gociano">Gociano</a>, Lord of Frisia, the Wendish March, Pordenone, Biscay, Molin, Salins, Tripoli and Mechelen.</i></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms_of_Charles_V">Coat of arms of Charles V</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Coat of arms of Charles V">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Coat of arms of Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Coat of arms of Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor</a></div>
<p>Coat of arms of Charles I of Spain and V of Germany according to the description: Arms of Charles I added to those of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">Castile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Leon" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Leon">Leon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Aragon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sicily" title="Kingdom of Sicily">Two Sicilies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Granada_(Crown_of_Castile)" title="Kingdom of Granada (Crown of Castile)">Granada</a> present in the previous coat, those of <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Austria" title="List of rulers of Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Burgundy" title="Duchy of Burgundy">ancient Burgundy</a>, modern Burgundy, <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brabant" title="Duchy of Brabant">Brabant</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_of_Flanders" title="County of Flanders">Flanders</a> and <a href="/wiki/County_of_Tyrol" title="County of Tyrol">Tyrol</a>. Charles I also incorporates the <a href="/wiki/Pillars_of_Hercules" title="Pillars of Hercules">pillars of Hercules</a> with the inscription "<a href="/wiki/Plus_ultra_(motto)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plus ultra (motto)">Plus Ultra</a>", representing the overseas empire and surrounding coat with the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Golden_Fleece" title="Order of the Golden Fleece">collar of the Golden Fleece</a>, as sovereign of the Order ringing the shield with the imperial crown and Acola double-headed eagle of the Holy Roman Empire and behind it the Spanish Cross of Burgundy. From 1520 added to the corresponding quarter to Aragon and Sicily, one in which the arms of Jerusalem, Naples and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">Navarre</a> are incorporated.</p>
