<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>References to Charles V include a large number of legends and folk tales; literary renderings of historical events connected to Charles's life and romantic adventures, his relationship to Flanders, and his abdication; and products marketed in his name.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>In <i>De heerelycke ende vrolycke daeden van Keyser Carel den V</i>, published by Joan de Grieck in 1674, the short stories, anecdotes, citations attributed to the emperor, and legends about his encounters with famous and ordinary people, depict a noble Christian monarch with a perfect cosmopolitan personality and a strong sense of humour. Converesely, in <a href="/wiki/Charles_De_Coster" title="Charles De Coster">Charles De Coster</a>'s masterpiece <i><a href="/wiki/The_Legend_of_Thyl_Ulenspiegel_and_Lamme_Goedzak" title="The Legend of Thyl Ulenspiegel and Lamme Goedzak">Thyl Ulenspiegel</a></i> (1867), after his death Charles V is consigned to Hell as punishment for the acts of the <a href="/wiki/Inquisition" title="Inquisition">Inquisition</a> under his rule, his punishment being that he would feel the pain of anyone tortured by the Inquisition. De Coster's book also mentions the story on the spectacles in the coat of arms of <a href="/wiki/Oudenaarde" title="Oudenaarde">Oudenaarde</a>, the one about a paysant of <a href="/wiki/Berchem" title="Berchem">Berchem</a> in <i>Het geuzenboek</i> (1979) by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Paul_Boon" title="Louis Paul Boon">Louis Paul Boon</a>, while <a href="/w/index.php?title=Abraham_Hans&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Abraham Hans (page does not exist)">Abraham Hans</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abraham_Hans" class="extiw" title="nl:Abraham Hans">nl</a>)</span> (1882–1939) included both tales in <i>De liefdesavonturen van keizer Karel in Vlaanderen</i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lord_Byron" title="Lord Byron">Lord Byron</a>'s <i>Ode to <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_Buonaparte" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon Buonaparte">Napoleon Buonaparte</a></i> refers to Charles as "The Spaniard".</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Escutcheon_of_Charlest_V_John_Singer_Sargent_1912.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Escutcheon_of_Charlest_V_John_Singer_Sargent_1912.jpeg/220px-Escutcheon_of_Charlest_V_John_Singer_Sargent_1912.jpeg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Escutcheon_of_Charlest_V_John_Singer_Sargent_1912.jpeg/330px-Escutcheon_of_Charlest_V_John_Singer_Sargent_1912.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Escutcheon_of_Charlest_V_John_Singer_Sargent_1912.jpeg/440px-Escutcheon_of_Charlest_V_John_Singer_Sargent_1912.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1168" data-file-height="766" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Escutcheon_of_Charlest_V_John_Singer_Sargent_1912.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Eschutcheon of Charles V</i>, watercolor, <a href="/wiki/John_Singer_Sargent" title="John Singer Sargent">John Singer Sargent</a>, 1912. <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art" title="Metropolitan Museum of Art">Metropolitan Museum of Art</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Charles V is a notable character in <a href="/wiki/Simone_de_Beauvoir" title="Simone de Beauvoir">Simone de Beauvoir</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/All_Men_Are_Mortal" title="All Men Are Mortal">All Men Are Mortal</a></i>.</li>
<li>In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Maltese_Falcon_(novel)" title="The Maltese Falcon (novel)">The Maltese Falcon</a></i>, the title object is said to have been an intended gift to Charles V.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plays">Plays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Plays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Charles V appears as a character in the play <i><a href="/wiki/Doctor_Faustus_(play)" title="Doctor Faustus (play)">Doctor Faustus</a></i> by the Elizabethan playwright <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Marlowe" title="Christopher Marlowe">Christopher Marlowe</a>. In Act 4 Scene 1 of the A Text, Faustus attends Court by the Emperor's request and with the assistance of <a href="/wiki/Mephistopheles" title="Mephistopheles">Mephistopheles</a> conjures up spirits representing <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> and his paramour as a demonstration of his magical powers.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opera">Opera</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Opera">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ernst_Krenek" title="Ernst Krenek">Ernst Krenek</a>'s opera <i><a href="/wiki/Karl_V" title="Karl V">Karl V</a></i> (opus 73, 1930) examines the title character's career via flashbacks.</li>
<li>In the third act of <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Verdi" title="Giuseppe Verdi">Giuseppe Verdi</a>'s opera <i><a href="/wiki/Ernani" title="Ernani">Ernani</a></i>, the election of Charles as Holy Roman Emperor is presented. Charles (Don Carlo in the opera) prays before the tomb of <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>. With the announcement that he is elected as Carlo Quinto he declares an amnesty including the eponymous bandit Ernani who had followed him there to murder him as a rival for the love of Elvira. The opera, based on the <a href="/wiki/Victor_Hugo" title="Victor Hugo">Victor Hugo</a> play <i><a href="/wiki/Hernani_(drama)" title="Hernani (drama)">Hernani</a></i>, portrays Charles as a callous and cynical adventurer whose character is transformed by the election into a responsible and clement ruler.</li>
<li>In another Verdi opera, <i><a href="/wiki/Don_Carlo" class="mw-redirect" title="Don Carlo">Don Carlo</a></i>, the final scene implies that it is Charles V, now living the last years of his life as a hermit, who rescues his grandson, Don Carlo, from his father <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II</a> and the Inquisition, by taking Carlo with him to his hermitage at the monastery in Yuste.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Food">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>A Flemish legend about Charles being served a beer at the village of <a href="/wiki/Olen,_Belgium" title="Olen, Belgium">Olen</a>, as well as the emperor's lifelong preference of beer above wine, led to the naming of several beer varieties in his honor. The <i>Haacht</i> Brewery of <a href="/wiki/Boortmeerbeek" title="Boortmeerbeek">Boortmeerbeek</a> produces Charles Quint, while <a href="/wiki/Het_Anker_Brewery" title="Het Anker Brewery">Het Anker Brewery</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mechelen" title="Mechelen">Mechelen</a> produces Gouden Carolus, including a Grand Cru of the Emperor, brewed once a year on Charles V's birthday.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Grupo Cruzcampo brews Legado De Yuste in honor of Charles and attributes the inspiration to his Flemish origin and his last days at the monastery of Yuste.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carlos_V_(candy_bar)" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlos V (candy bar)">Carlos V</a> is the name of a popular chocolate bar in Mexico. Its tagline is "El Rey de los Chocolates" or "The King of Chocolates" and "Carlos V, El Emperador del Chocolate" or "Charles V, the Emperor of Chocolates."</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="TV_and_Film">TV and Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: TV and Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Charles V is portrayed by Torben Liebrecht and is figured prominently in the 2003 film <i><a href="/wiki/Luther_(2003_film)" title="Luther (2003 film)">Luther</a></i> covering the life of <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> up until the <a href="/wiki/Diet_of_Augsburg" title="Diet of Augsburg">Diet of Augsburg</a>.</li>
<li>Charles V is portrayed in one episode of the Showtime series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tudors" title="The Tudors">The Tudors</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Armesto" title="Sebastian Armesto">Sebastian Armesto</a>.</li>
<li>Charles V is the main subject of the <a href="/wiki/Televisi%C3%B3n_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Televisión Española">TVE</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/Carlos,_Rey_Emperador" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlos, Rey Emperador">Carlos, Rey Emperador</a></i> and is portrayed by Álvaro Cervantes.</li>
</ul>
